# PART I: PROJECT OVERVIEW

## 1.1 Document Purpose

This document serves as the **single source of truth** for all TERAS-LANG research decisions. Any Claude instance working on TERAS-LANG MUST:

1. **READ** this document fully before any implementation
2. **FOLLOW** all decisions marked Ã¢Å“â€¦ Approved
3. **UPDATE** this document with new research findings
4. **MAINTAIN** traceability to research sessions

## 1.2 TERAS Ecosystem Context

TERAS-LANG is the implementation language for the TERAS security platform, consisting of:

| Product | Full Name | Domain |
|---------|-----------|--------|
| **MENARA** | Mobile Enterprise Network Adaptive Response Architecture | Mobile Security |
| **GAPURA** | Gateway Application Protection Unified Response Architecture | Web Application Firewall |
| **ZIRAH** | Zero-trust Intelligent Response Anomaly Handler | Endpoint Detection & Response |
| **BENTENG** | Biometric Enterprise Network Trust Engine | eKYC/Identity Verification |
| **BENTENG-SDK** | BENTENG Software Development Kit | Client-side SDK for customer apps |
| **SANDI** | Secure Authentication & Digital Identity | Digital Signatures |
| **SARAF** | Distributed Neural Command Mesh | Inter-node coordination |
| **NADI** | Byzantine Fault-Tolerant Pulse Network | Health & consensus |
| **JEJAK** | Append-only Audit Logging System | Immutable audit trails |

## 1.4 Pre-Phase Mandates

Before Phase 0.5 and Phase 1 proceed, the following IMMUTABLE MANDATES have been established:

| Decision | Name | Status |
|----------|------|--------|
| **D37** | Threat Defense Mandate | Ã¢Å“â€¦ Approved |
| **D38** | Performance Mandate | Ã¢Å“â€¦ Approved |
| **D46** | Malay Naming Convention Strategy | Ã¢Å“â€¦ Approved |

These mandates govern ALL subsequent design decisions and cannot be weakened.

## 1.5 Document Conventions

- **Session References:** "Session N" refers to research session number N
- **Decision References:** "DN" refers to design decision number N
- **Status Markers:**
  - Ã¢Å“â€¦ Approved: Decision finalized and binding
  - Ã°Å¸â€œâ€¹ Specified: Session/decision designed but not yet executed
  - Ã°Å¸â€â€ž In Progress: Currently being researched
  - Ã¢Ââ€œ Open: Requires further research
- **Malay Terms:** TERAS uses Malay naming for products and concepts (see D46)

# PART II: TYPE THEORY FOUNDATIONS

## 2.1 MARTIN-LÃƒâ€“F TYPE THEORY (MLTT)

**Source:** Sessions 1-3 | Per Martin-LÃƒÂ¶f (1971-1984)

### Core Judgments

```
ÃŽâ€œ Ã¢Å Â¢ A type        A is a well-formed type in context ÃŽâ€œ
ÃŽâ€œ Ã¢Å Â¢ a : A         a has type A in context ÃŽâ€œ
ÃŽâ€œ Ã¢Å Â¢ A = B type    A and B are equal types
ÃŽâ€œ Ã¢Å Â¢ a = b : A     a and b are equal terms of type A
```

### Dependent Types

```
ÃŽÂ -type (Dependent Function):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Generalizes: A Ã¢â€ â€™ B when B doesn't mention x
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Example: (n : Nat) Ã¢â€ â€™ Vec n Int  (vector of exactly n integers)

              ÃŽâ€œ Ã¢Å Â¢ ÃŽÂ»x.b : ÃŽÂ (x:A).B

              Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
                    ÃŽâ€œ Ã¢Å Â¢ f(a) : B[a/x]

ÃŽÂ£-type (Dependent Pair):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
ÃŽÂ£(x:A).B[x]   or   (x : A) Ãƒâ€” B[x]

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Second component's type depends on first component's value
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Generalizes: A Ãƒâ€” B when B doesn't mention x
```

### Universe Hierarchy

```
TypeÃ¢â€šâ‚¬ : TypeÃ¢â€šÂ : TypeÃ¢â€šâ€š : TypeÃ¢â€šÆ’ : ...

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Avoids Russell's paradox (Type : Type is inconsistent)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Universe polymorphism: Ã¢Ë†â‚¬ i. Type_i Ã¢â€ â€™ Type_i
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Cumulative: Type_i Ã¢Å â€  Type_{i+1}

TERAS-LANG Implication:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Need universe hierarchy for consistency
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Consider universe polymorphism for usability
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ May use typical ambiguity (implicit levels)
```

```
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Inductive type definitions
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Pattern matching
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Fixpoint definitions with termination checking
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Universe hierarchy

Inductive Type Schema:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Inductive T (params) : indices Ã¢â€ â€™ Type :=
  | CÃ¢â€šÂ : argsÃ¢â€šÂ Ã¢â€ â€™ T ...
  | CÃ¢â€šâ€š : argsÃ¢â€šâ€š Ã¢â€ â€™ T ...
  ...

Positivity Requirement:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ T must appear only in POSITIVE positions in constructor args
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Ensures consistency (no paradoxes)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Negative: (T Ã¢â€ â€™ X) Ã¢â€ â€™ T  -- FORBIDDEN
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Positive: X Ã¢â€ â€™ T, T Ãƒâ€” X  -- OK
```

### Termination Checking

```
Structural Recursion:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Fixpoint f (n : Nat) : T :=
  match n with
  | zero => base_case
  | succ m => ... f m ...  (* m is structurally smaller than n *)
  end.

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Guard condition: recursive call on structurally smaller arg
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Ensures termination of all functions
```

### Prop vs Set/Type

```
Prop Universe:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Proof irrelevance: All proofs of P : Prop are equal
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Cannot eliminate into computational types
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Erasable at runtime
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Example: Ã¢Ë†Æ’ proofs, equality proofs

Set/Type Universe:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Computationally relevant
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Can be pattern matched, extracted to code
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Not erasable
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Example: Nat, List, functions

Elimination Restriction:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Can eliminate Prop into Prop
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Can eliminate Set into Set or Prop
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Cannot eliminate Prop into Set (would leak proof info)

Exception: Singleton elimination
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ If P : Prop has exactly one constructor with Prop arguments
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Can eliminate into Set
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Example: True, And, Exists (when existential is Prop)
```

### TERAS-LANG IMPLICATIONS FROM TYPE THEORY

```

Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬

Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Full ÃŽÂ -types (dependent functions)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Full ÃŽÂ£-types (dependent pairs)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Identity types with J-eliminator
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Consider HoTT-style equality later

DECISION 3: Inductive Types
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Positive inductive types with eliminators
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Pattern matching as derived form
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Termination checking via structural recursion
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Guard condition similar to Coq

DECISION 4: Computation
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Strong normalization required
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ ÃŽÂ²-reduction as primary computation rule
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ ÃŽÂ·-expansion for functions and pairs
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Definitional vs propositional equality distinction
```

# PART III: LINEAR & SUBSTRUCTURAL TYPES

### Linear Logic Connectives

```
A Ã¢Å â€” B    Tensor (both, separately)

Ã¢Å Â¥        Multiplicative false

Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬

Ã¢Å Â¤        Additive unit (anything works)
```

### Linear Types in Practice

```
Rust-Style Ownership:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
fn consume(s: String) { ... }      // Takes ownership (linear use)
fn borrow(s: &String) { ... }      // Borrows (doesn't consume)
fn mut_borrow(s: &mut String) { }  // Exclusive mutable borrow

let s = String::from("hello");
consume(s);
// s is now moved (linear), cannot use again

Linear Haskell (GHC 9.0+):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
f :: a %1 -> b          -- Linear function: must use 'a' exactly once
g :: a %Many -> b       -- Unrestricted: can use 'a' any number of times
h :: a %p -> b          -- Polymorphic: multiplicity 'p' determined by caller

-- File handle example
withFile :: FilePath -> (Handle %1 -> IO a) %1 -> IO a
-- Guarantees handle is used exactly once (closed properly)

Clean's Uniqueness Types:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
*World Ã¢â€ â€™ (*World, a)    -- Unique world, must thread through
*Array Ã¢â€ â€™ (*Array, Int)  -- In-place array update

-- Uniqueness allows safe in-place mutation
update :: *{Int} Int Int -> *{Int}
```

## 3.2 RUST OWNERSHIP MODEL (Deep Dive)

**Source:** Session 10 | Rust Language

### Ownership Rules

```
RULE 1: Each value has exactly one owner
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
let s1 = String::from("hello");
let s2 = s1;  // s1 is MOVED to s2
// println!("{}", s1);  // ERROR: s1 no longer valid

RULE 2: When owner goes out of scope, value is dropped
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
{
    let s = String::from("hello");
}  // s goes out of scope, memory freed (drop called)

RULE 3: References must not outlive referent
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
fn invalid() -> &String {
    let s = String::from("hello");
    &s  // ERROR: s will be dropped, reference would dangle
}
```

### Borrowing Rules

```
IMMUTABLE BORROWS (&T):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Multiple immutable borrows allowed simultaneously
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Cannot mutate through immutable borrow
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Original owner cannot mutate while immutable borrows exist

let s = String::from("hello");
let r1 = &s;  // OK
let r2 = &s;  // OK: multiple immutable borrows
// s.push_str(" world");  // ERROR: cannot mutate while borrowed

MUTABLE BORROWS (&mut T):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Only ONE mutable borrow at a time
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ No other borrows (mutable or immutable) while mutable borrow exists
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Original owner cannot access while mutably borrowed

let mut s = String::from("hello");
let r = &mut s;
// let r2 = &s;      // ERROR: cannot borrow immutably
// let r3 = &mut s;  // ERROR: cannot borrow mutably twice
r.push_str(" world");
```

### Lifetimes

```
EXPLICIT LIFETIMES:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
fn longest<'a>(x: &'a str, y: &'a str) -> &'a str {
    if x.len() > y.len() { x } else { y }
}
// Return value lives as long as BOTH inputs

LIFETIME ELISION RULES:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
1. Each input reference gets its own lifetime
2. If one input lifetime, output gets that lifetime
3. If &self or &mut self, output gets self's lifetime

// These are equivalent:
fn first_word(s: &str) -> &str
fn first_word<'a>(s: &'a str) -> &'a str

LIFETIME BOUNDS:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
T: 'a           // T must live at least as long as 'a
T: 'static      // T must live for entire program
'a: 'b          // 'a must outlive 'b
```

### MIR (Mid-level Intermediate Representation)

```
Source Ã¢â€ â€™ HIR Ã¢â€ â€™ MIR Ã¢â€ â€™ LLVM IR Ã¢â€ â€™ Machine Code

MIR Purpose:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit control flow (no hidden drops)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit moves and borrows
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Borrow checking happens here
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Optimization (inlining, constant folding)

MIR Example:
fn example(x: i32) -> i32 {
    x + 1
}

// MIR:
fn example(_1: i32) -> i32 {
    let mut _0: i32;
    bb0: {
        _0 = Add(_1, const 1_i32);
        return;
    }
}

Key MIR Concepts:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Basic blocks (bb0, bb1, ...)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Places (_0, _1, _2, ...)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Statements and terminators
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit drops and moves
```

### Borrow Checker Internals (Polonius)

```
Non-Lexical Lifetimes (NLL):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Lifetimes based on control flow, not lexical scope
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ More permissive than original borrow checker

let mut x = 5;
let y = &x;      // borrow of x starts
println!("{}", y);
// y is no longer used after this point
x = 6;           // OK with NLL: y's lifetime ended

Polonius Algorithm:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Datalog-based borrow checker
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Computes "origin" of each reference
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Tracks which references are "live"
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ More precise than NLL

Key Relations:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ loan_issued_at(loan, point)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ loan_invalidated_at(loan, point)  
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ origin_contains_loan_on_entry(origin, loan, point)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ loan_live_at(loan, point)

Error if:
loan_invalidated_at(L, P) Ã¢Ë†Â§ loan_live_at(L, P)
```

## 3.3 ZIG SAFETY MODEL

**Source:** Session 11 | Zig Language

### Comptime (Compile-Time Execution)

```
const std = @import("std");

// Comptime function execution
fn fibonacci(n: u32) u32 {
    if (n < 2) return n;
    return fibonacci(n - 1) + fibonacci(n - 2);
}

// Computed at compile time
const fib_10 = comptime fibonacci(10);  // 55 at compile time

// Comptime type manipulation
fn Matrix(comptime T: type, comptime rows: usize, comptime cols: usize) type {
    return [rows][cols]T;
}

const Mat3x3 = Matrix(f32, 3, 3);  // [3][3]f32

// Comptime string formatting
fn generateStruct(comptime name: []const u8) type {
    return @Type(.{
        .Struct = .{
            .layout = .Auto,
            .fields = &[_]std.builtin.Type.StructField{
                .{
                    .name = name,
                    .type = i32,
                    .default_value = null,
                    .is_comptime = false,
                    .alignment = 0,
                },
            },
            .decls = &[_]std.builtin.Type.Declaration{},
            .is_tuple = false,
        },
    });
}
```

### Runtime Safety Checks

```
Debug Mode Safety (ReleaseSafe keeps many):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Integer overflow detection
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Bounds checking on arrays/slices
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Null pointer dereference detection
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Unwrap of null optionals
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Unreachable code detection

// Overflow detection
var x: u8 = 255;
x += 1;  // panic in debug: integer overflow

// Bounds checking
var arr = [_]i32{1, 2, 3};
_ = arr[5];  // panic: index out of bounds

// Optional unwrap
var maybe: ?i32 = null;
_ = maybe.?;  // panic: unwrap of null

Safety Annotations:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
@setRuntimeSafety(false)  // Disable for block
@intCast(u8, big_value)   // Checked cast
@truncate(u8, big_value)  // Explicit truncation
```

### Allocator Interface

```
// General Purpose Allocator with safety features
var gpa = std.heap.GeneralPurposeAllocator(.{
    .safety = true,                    // Enable safety checks
    .stack_trace_frames = 10,          // Stack traces on error
    .enable_memory_limit = true,       // Memory limits
    .thread_safe = true,               // Thread safety
}){};
defer _ = gpa.deinit();  // Detect leaks on exit

const allocator = gpa.allocator();

// Allocation with explicit failure handling
const ptr = allocator.alloc(u8, 1024) catch |err| {
    // Handle allocation failure
    return err;
};
defer allocator.free(ptr);  // Guaranteed cleanup

// Arena allocator (bulk free)
var arena = std.heap.ArenaAllocator.init(std.heap.page_allocator);
defer arena.deinit();

// Failing allocator for testing
const failing = std.testing.failing_allocator;
```

## 3.4 TERAS-LANG IMPLICATIONS FROM LINEAR TYPES

```
DECISION 5: Linear Type System
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Affine by default (use at most once)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Linear annotation for "must use exactly once"
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Unrestricted annotation for copyable types
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Syntax: Ãâ€ž %1 (linear), Ãâ€ž %Ãâ€° (unrestricted), Ãâ€ž %a (affine)

DECISION 6: Ownership Model
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Single owner principle (like Rust)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Move semantics by default
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Borrowing for temporary access
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Mutable borrows exclusive

DECISION 7: Lifetime System
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Region-based lifetimes
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit when needed, elided when unambiguous
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ NLL-style flow-sensitive analysis
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Consider Polonius-style precision

DECISION 8: Comptime Integration
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Compile-time function execution (like Zig)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Type-level computation
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Comptime parameters for generics
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Staged computation where beneficial

DECISION 9: Safety Guarantees
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Memory safety by default (no null, no dangling)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Bounds checking in debug mode
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Overflow checking configurable
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit unsafe escape hatch with proof obligations
```

# PART IV: REFINEMENT TYPES & SMT VERIFICATION

## 4.1 REFINEMENT TYPES THEORY

**Source:** Sessions 5-7, 20-21 | Liquid Haskell, F*, Flux, Dafny, Why3

### Basic Refinement Types

```
Definition:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
{ v : B | Ãâ€ (v) }

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ B is base type
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Ãâ€  is logical predicate (refinement)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ v is value being refined
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Type inhabited only by values satisfying Ãâ€ 

Examples:
{ v : Int | v > 0 }           -- Positive integers
{ v : Int | v >= 0 && v < n } -- Bounded integers
{ v : List a | len v > 0 }    -- Non-empty lists
{ v : Int | v == x + y }      -- Computed value

Subtyping:
{ v : B | Ãâ€  } <: { v : B | ÃË† }  iff  Ã¢Ë†â‚¬v. Ãâ€ (v) Ã¢Å¸Â¹ ÃË†(v)

{ v : Int | v > 5 } <: { v : Int | v > 0 }  -- OK: v > 5 Ã¢Å¸Â¹ v > 0
```

### Liquid Types (Decidable Refinement Types)

```
Key Insight: Restrict refinements to decidable logic

Liquid Type Grammar:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ãâ€ž ::= { v : B | r }           -- Refined base type
r ::= ÃŽÂº | r Ã¢Ë†Â§ r               -- Refinements
ÃŽÂº ::= e relop e               -- Atomic predicates
e ::= x | c | e + e | e - e   -- Linear arithmetic

QF-LIA (Quantifier-Free Linear Integer Arithmetic):
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Decidable by SMT solvers
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Supports: +, -, <, Ã¢â€°Â¤, =, Ã¢â€°Â , Ã¢Ë†Â§, Ã¢Ë†Â¨, Ã‚Â¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Does NOT support: *, /, quantifiers

Inference Algorithm:
1. Generate fresh predicate variables
2. Collect subtyping constraints
3. Solve via liquid fixpoint algorithm
4. Report error if no solution
```

### F* Dependent Effects

```fstar
// Effect system with pre/post conditions
effect ST (a:Type) (pre:mem Ã¢â€ â€™ Type0) (post:mem Ã¢â€ â€™ a Ã¢â€ â€™ mem Ã¢â€ â€™ Type0) =
  STATE a (fun m0 p Ã¢â€ â€™ pre m0 Ã¢Ë†Â§ (Ã¢Ë†â‚¬x m1. post m0 x m1 Ã¢â€ â€™ p x m1))

// Verified stateful function
val incr : r:ref int Ã¢â€ â€™ ST unit
  (requires fun h Ã¢â€ â€™ h `contains` r)
  (ensures  fun h0 _ h1 Ã¢â€ â€™ h1 == upd h0 r (sel h0 r + 1))
let incr r = r := !r + 1

// Inductive types with indices
type vec (a:Type) : nat -> Type =
  | Nil : vec a 0
  | Cons : #n:nat -> hd:a -> tl:vec a n -> vec a (n + 1)

// SMT-backed verification
val append_length: #a:Type -> #m:nat -> #n:nat ->
                   v1:vec a m -> v2:vec a n ->
                   Lemma (length (append v1 v2) == m + n)
```

### Flux (Rust Refinement Types)

```rust
// Basic refinements
#[flux::sig(fn(x: i32{x > 0}) -> i32{v: v > 0})]
fn abs_positive(x: i32) -> i32 {
    x
}

// Indexed types
#[flux::refined_by(len: int)]
struct RVec<T> {
    inner: Vec<T>,
}

// Refined method
#[flux::sig(fn(&RVec<T>[@n], i: usize{i < n}) -> &T)]
fn get<T>(vec: &RVec<T>, i: usize) -> &T {
    &vec.inner[i]
}

// Strong updates (ownership-aware refinements)
#[flux::sig(fn(x: &strg i32[@n]) -> i32[n + 1] ensures x: i32[n + 1])]
fn incr(x: &mut i32) -> i32 {
    *x += 1;
    *x
}

// Path-sensitive refinements
#[flux::sig(fn(b: bool, x: i32{b => x > 0}) -> i32{v: b => v > 0})]
fn conditional(b: bool, x: i32) -> i32 {
    if b { x } else { 0 }
}
```

## 4.2 DAFNY VERIFICATION

**Source:** Session 20 | Microsoft Research

### Core Verification Model

```dafny
// Method with pre/post conditions
method BinarySearch(a: array<int>, key: int) returns (index: int)
  requires forall i, j :: 0 <= i < j < a.Length ==> a[i] <= a[j]  // Sorted
  ensures index >= 0 ==> index < a.Length && a[index] == key
  ensures index < 0 ==> forall i :: 0 <= i < a.Length ==> a[i] != key
{
  var lo, hi := 0, a.Length;
  while lo < hi
    invariant 0 <= lo <= hi <= a.Length
    invariant forall i :: 0 <= i < lo ==> a[i] < key
    invariant forall i :: hi <= i < a.Length ==> a[i] > key
  {
    var mid := (lo + hi) / 2;
    if a[mid] < key {
      lo := mid + 1;
    } else if a[mid] > key {
      hi := mid;
    } else {
      return mid;
    }
  }
  return -1;
}

// Ghost code (specification only)
ghost function Sum(a: seq<int>): int
{
  if |a| == 0 then 0 else a[0] + Sum(a[1..])
}

// Lemma (proof as code)
lemma SumAppend(a: seq<int>, b: seq<int>)
  ensures Sum(a + b) == Sum(a) + Sum(b)
{
  if a == [] {
    assert a + b == b;
  } else {
    calc {
      Sum(a + b);
      == a[0] + Sum((a + b)[1..]);
      == { assert (a + b)[1..] == a[1..] + b; }
         a[0] + Sum(a[1..] + b);
      == { SumAppend(a[1..], b); }
         a[0] + Sum(a[1..]) + Sum(b);
      == Sum(a) + Sum(b);
    }
  }
}
```

### Proof Stability Challenges

```
Dafny Proof Brittleness:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Problem: SMT solvers are non-deterministic
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Same code may verify one day, fail the next
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Z3 heuristics sensitive to small changes
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Timeout-dependent behavior

Causes:
1. Quantifier instantiation order
2. E-matching trigger selection
3. Random seeds in solver
4. Heap scrambling effects

Mitigations:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ {:vcs_split_on_every_assert} - Split VCs
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ {:opaque} - Hide function definitions until needed
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ reveal/hide commands - Control unfolding
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit triggers: forall x {:trigger f(x)} :: P(x)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ calc statements - Guide arithmetic reasoning
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ assert-assume chains - Break complex proofs
```

## 4.3 WHY3 MULTI-PROVER PLATFORM

### Architecture Overview


### WhyML Language

```ocaml
(* Module with specification *)
module BinarySearch
  use int.Int
  use array.Array

  (* Predicate for sorted array *)
  predicate sorted (a: array int) =
    forall i j. 0 <= i <= j < length a -> a[i] <= a[j]

  (* Binary search with full specification *)
  let binary_search (a: array int) (v: int) : int
    requires { sorted a }
    ensures  { result >= 0 -> 0 <= result < length a /\ a[result] = v }
    ensures  { result < 0 -> forall i. 0 <= i < length a -> a[i] <> v }
  =
    let ref lo = 0 in
    let ref hi = length a in
    while lo < hi do
      invariant { 0 <= lo <= hi <= length a }
      invariant { forall i. 0 <= i < lo -> a[i] < v }
      invariant { forall i. hi <= i < length a -> a[i] > v }
      variant   { hi - lo }
      let mid = lo + (hi - lo) / 2 in
      if a[mid] < v then
        lo <- mid + 1
      else if a[mid] > v then
        hi <- mid
      else
        return mid
    done;
    return (-1)
end
```

### Proof Strategies

```
(* Proof strategy language *)
let my_strategy = 
  c Alt-Ergo 1 |           (* Try Alt-Ergo with 1s timeout *)
  c Z3 1 |                  (* Try Z3 with 1s timeout *)
  t split_vc;               (* Split verification condition *)
  c Alt-Ergo 5 |           (* Retry with 5s timeout *)
  c CVC4 5 |
  t introduce_premises;     (* Introduce premises *)
  t inline_goal;           (* Inline definitions *)
  c Z3 30 | c CVC4 30       (* Long timeout, parallel *)

(* Auto level strategies *)
(* Level 0: Quick provers, short timeouts *)
(* Level 1: Split VCs, medium timeouts *)
(* Level 2: All transformations, long timeouts, Coq fallback *)
```

## 4.4 TERAS-LANG IMPLICATIONS FROM REFINEMENT TYPES

```
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Refinement types as primary specification mechanism
```

### Frame Rule

```
              {P} c {Q}
         Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬ (Frame)
         {P Ã¢Ë†â€” R} c {Q Ã¢Ë†â€” R}

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ If c only touches memory in P
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Then R (the "frame") is PRESERVED
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Enables MODULAR verification

Example:
{x Ã¢â€ Â¦ 5} *x := 7 {x Ã¢â€ Â¦ 7}
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬ (Frame with y Ã¢â€ Â¦ 10)
{x Ã¢â€ Â¦ 5 Ã¢Ë†â€” y Ã¢â€ Â¦ 10} *x := 7 {x Ã¢â€ Â¦ 7 Ã¢Ë†â€” y Ã¢â€ Â¦ 10}

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ y is unchanged because it's in the frame
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ No need to mention y in the proof of *x := 7
```

### Concurrent Separation Logic

```

    {PÃ¢â€šÂ Ã¢Ë†â€” PÃ¢â€šâ€š} cÃ¢â€šÂ || cÃ¢â€šâ€š {QÃ¢â€šÂ Ã¢Ë†â€” QÃ¢â€šâ€š}

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Disjoint heaps Ã¢Å¸Â¹ no data races
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ cÃ¢â€šÂ owns PÃ¢â€šÂ, cÃ¢â€šâ€š owns PÃ¢â€šâ€š
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ They cannot interfere (PÃ¢â€šÂ Ã¢Ë†â€” PÃ¢â€šâ€š means disjoint)

CRITICAL SECTION:
{inv(L) Ã¢Ë†â€” P} with L do { c } {inv(L) Ã¢Ë†â€” Q}
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Lock L protects invariant inv(L)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Inside critical section: access inv(L)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Must restore inv(L) before releasing
```

### Iris Proof Mode (Coq Tactics)

```coq
Lemma example : {{{ P Ã¢Ë†â€” Q }}} e {{{ v, RET v; R v }}}.

  iIntros "[HP HQ]".           (* Split Ã¢Ë†â€” into hypotheses *)
  iDestruct "HP" as "#HP".     (* Make persistent *)
  wp_bind (inner_expr).        (* Focus on subexpr *)
  iApply "HQ".                 (* Apply hypothesis *)
  iFrame "HP".                 (* Frame out HP *)
  iSplitL "HQ".                (* Split goal *)

```

```
Ã¢â€â€š (tag1, Uniq)Ã¢â€â€š Ã¢â€ Â Bottom (original owner)
Ã¢â€â€Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€Ëœ

RULES:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Creating &mut: Push (new_tag, Unique)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Creating &: Push (new_tag, SharedReadOnly)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Using pointer: Find tag in stack (else UB)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Writing: Pop everything above the item

EXAMPLE:
let mut x = 42;
let y = &mut x;    // Stack: [(x, Uniq), (y, Uniq)]
let z = &*y;       // Stack: [(x, Uniq), (y, Uniq), (z, SRO)]
*y = 43;           // Pop z (invalidated), use y
// z is now invalid!
```

# PART VI: FORMAL VERIFICATION & VERIFIED COMPILERS

## 6.1 SPARK/ADA VERIFICATION

**Source:** Sessions 8-9, 16-17 | AdaCore

### SPARK Contracts

```ada
package Stack with SPARK_Mode is
   Max_Size : constant := 100;
   
   type Stack is private;
   
   function Is_Empty (S : Stack) return Boolean;
   function Is_Full (S : Stack) return Boolean;
   function Size (S : Stack) return Natural;
   
   procedure Push (S : in out Stack; Item : Integer)
     with Pre  => not Is_Full (S),
          Post => not Is_Empty (S) and Size (S) = Size (S'Old) + 1;
   
   procedure Pop (S : in out Stack)
     with Pre  => not Is_Empty (S),
          Post => not Is_Full (S);

private
   type Element_Array is array (1 .. Max_Size) of Integer;
   
   type Stack is record
      Data : Element_Array;
      Size : Natural := 0;
   end record
     with Type_Invariant => Size <= Max_Size;
end Stack;
```

### GNATprove Verification

```
ANALYSIS LEVELS:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Stone:   Check SPARK subset conformance
Bronze:  Prove absence of runtime errors
Silver:  Prove functional correctness (key properties)
Gold:    Prove full functional correctness
Platinum: Prove with Coq for complex properties

PROOF FLOW:
Source Ã¢â€ â€™ Why3 VCs Ã¢â€ â€™ Alt-Ergo/Z3/CVC4 Ã¢â€ â€™ Coq (if needed)

CONTRACT ANNOTATIONS:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Pre => condition               -- Precondition
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Post => condition              -- Postcondition  
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Contract_Cases => (...)        -- Disjoint cases
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Global => (In => X, Out => Y)  -- State dependencies
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Depends => (X => Y)            -- Information flow

```

# PART VII: ZERO-KNOWLEDGE PROOF SYSTEMS

## 7.1 R1CS AND GROTH16

**Source:** Sessions 12-15 | Circom, Noir, Leo, Cairo

### Rank-1 Constraint Systems

```
R1CS FORM:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
(A Ã‚Â· w) Ã¢Ë†Ëœ (B Ã‚Â· w) = C Ã‚Â· w

Where:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ w = (1, public_inputs, private_inputs, intermediate)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ A, B, C are sparse matrices
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Ã¢Ë†Ëœ is element-wise multiplication
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ All operations in finite field F_p

EXAMPLE (x * y = z):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
w = (1, z, x, y)

A = [0, 0, 1, 0]  -- Select x
B = [0, 0, 0, 1]  -- Select y
C = [0, 1, 0, 0]  -- Select z

Constraint: x * y = z

ARITHMETIC CIRCUIT Ã¢â€ â€™ R1CS:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Each multiplication gate Ã¢â€ â€™ one constraint
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Addition gates are "free" (linear combinations)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Every operation must be quadratic
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Non-native ops (comparison, division) require gadgets
```

### Groth16 Protocol

```

Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Generate toxic waste Ãâ€ž
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Compute proving key pk
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Compute verification key vk
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ MUST destroy Ãâ€ž (MPC ceremony)

PROVE (Prover):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Input: circuit, witness, pk
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Compute polynomial evaluations
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Create elliptic curve proof
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Output: Ãâ‚¬ = (A, B, C) Ã¢Ë†Ë† GÃ¢â€šÂ Ãƒâ€” GÃ¢â€šâ€š Ãƒâ€” GÃ¢â€šÂ

VERIFY (Verifier):
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Input: public inputs, proof, vk
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Check pairing equation
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ e(A, B) = e(ÃŽÂ±, ÃŽÂ²) Ã‚Â· e(vk_ÃŽÂ³, ÃŽÂ³) Ã‚Â· e(C, ÃŽÂ´)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ O(1) time, ~200 bytes proof

PROPERTIES:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Proof size: Constant (~200 bytes)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Verification: Constant time
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Trusted setup: Per-circuit (not universal)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Quantum: NOT secure (pairing-based)
```

### PLONK and Variants

```
PLONK ADVANTAGES:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Universal trusted setup (one ceremony for all circuits)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ More flexible constraint system
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Custom gates possible

PLONK CONSTRAINT:
q_L Ã‚Â· a + q_R Ã‚Â· b + q_O Ã‚Â· c + q_M Ã‚Â· (aÃ‚Â·b) + q_C = 0

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ q_L, q_R, q_O, q_M, q_C: Selector polynomials
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ a, b, c: Wire values
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Can express any gate

FFLONK:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Further optimized PLONK
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Smaller proof size
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Faster verification
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Used by Polygon zkEVM
```

## 7.2 ZK DSL LANGUAGES

**Source:** Sessions 12-15 | Circom, Noir, Leo, Cairo

### Circom

```javascript
// Template definition (like a function)
template Multiplier2() {
    signal input a;
    signal input b;
    signal output c;
    
    c <== a * b;  // Constraint: c = a * b
}

// Quadratic constraint operators
c <== a * b;     // c = a * b AND constrain
c <-- a * b;     // c = a * b (assignment only, no constraint!)
c === a * b;     // Just constrain (c already assigned)

// Template instantiation
template Main() {
    signal input in1;
    signal input in2;
    signal output out;
    
    component mul = Multiplier2();
    mul.a <== in1;
    mul.b <== in2;
    out <== mul.c;
}
```

### Noir (Aztec)

```rust
// Noir looks like Rust but compiles to ZK circuits

// Function with constraints
fn main(x: Field, y: Field) -> pub Field {
    let z = x * y;
    assert(z != 0);  // Becomes constraint
    z
}

// Public vs private
fn verify(pub public_input: Field, private_secret: Field) {
    assert(hash(private_secret) == public_input);
}

// Recursive proofs
fn verify_recursive(proof: Proof, vk: VerificationKey) {
    std::verify_proof(vk, proof);
}
```

### Leo (Aleo)

```leo
// Leo program with records (private state)
program token.aleo {
    record Token {
        owner: address,
        amount: u64,
    }
    
    // Private function (full ZK)
    transition transfer(
        sender: Token,
        receiver: address,
        amount: u64
    ) -> (Token, Token) {
        assert(sender.amount >= amount);
        
        let remaining = Token {
            owner: sender.owner,
            amount: sender.amount - amount,
        };
        let transferred = Token {
            owner: receiver,
            amount: amount,
        };
        return (remaining, transferred);
    }
}
```

# PART VIII: SECURITY FOUNDATIONS

## 8.1 INFORMATION FLOW CONTROL (IFC)

**Source:** Session 18 | Denning, Myers

### Security Lattice

```
LATTICE STRUCTURE:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
          Top (Ã¢Å Â¤)
         /   |   \
     Secret  |   Admin
         \   |   /
        Confidential
             |
          Public
             |
        Bottom (Ã¢Å Â¥)

Properties:
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Ã¢Å â€˜ defines "can flow to"
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Public Ã¢Å â€˜ Secret (public data can become secret)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Ã‚Â¬(Secret Ã¢Å â€˜ Public) (secret cannot become public)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Meet (Ã¢Å â€œ): least upper bound
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Join (Ã¢Å â€): greatest lower bound
```

### JIF/Jflow Model

```java
// Security labels on types
int{AliceÃ¢â€ â€™Bob} x;       // Alice owns, Bob can read
int{AliceÃ¢â€ â€™*; AliceÃ¢â€ Â*} y; // Alice controls reads/writes

// Principal hierarchy
principal Alice;
principal Bob;
principal Admin actsfor Alice, Bob;  // Admin subsumes both

// Declassification (explicit downgrade)
int{Public} z = declassify(x, {Public}) 
                 where authority(Alice);
// Only Alice can declassify her data

// Information flow rules
int{Alice} a = ...;
int{Bob} b = ...;
int{Alice Ã¢Å â€ Bob} c = a + b;  // Join of labels
// c is labeled with least restrictive label that protects both
```

### Noninterference

```
FORMAL DEFINITION:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
For program P, security levels L and H where L Ã¢Å â€˜ H:

P is noninterfering iff:
Ã¢Ë†â‚¬ lÃ¢â€šÂ, lÃ¢â€šâ€š : Low. Ã¢Ë†â‚¬ hÃ¢â€šÂ, hÃ¢â€šâ€š : High.
  P(lÃ¢â€šÂ, hÃ¢â€šÂ) =_L P(lÃ¢â€šâ€š, hÃ¢â€šâ€š)

"High inputs don't affect low outputs"

IMPLICIT FLOWS:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
if (secret) then
    public := 1
else
    public := 0

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Leaks secret via control flow
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ IFC must track implicit flows
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Typing rules prevent this

TERMINATION CHANNELS:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
while (secret) do skip

Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Leaks information via termination
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Termination-sensitive vs insensitive
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ TERAS-LANG: termination-insensitive default
```

## 8.2 CAPABILITY SECURITY

**Source:** Session 19 | Miller, E Language

### Object Capabilities

```
PRINCIPLES:
Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬
1. NO AMBIENT AUTHORITY
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ No global variables
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ No static mutable state
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ All resources via explicit parameters

2. CAPABILITIES ARE UNFORGEABLE REFERENCES
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Cannot create from integer
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Cannot guess valid capability
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Linear types enforce single-use

3. ATTENUATION
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Can create weaker capability from stronger
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Cannot amplify: read-only Ã¢â€ â€™ read-write Ã¢Å“â€”
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Principle of least privilege

4. CONFINEMENT
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Module cannot leak capabilities it doesn't have
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit capability passing at boundaries
   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ No implicit ambient access
```

### E Language Patterns

```javascript
// Sealer/Unsealer pattern (abstract types via capabilities)
def makeBrandPair() {
    def [sealer, unsealer] := makeBrand()
    return [sealer, unsealer]
}

let [seal, unseal] := makeBrandPair()
let box = seal(secret)      // Only holder of unseal can open
let value = unseal(box)     // Recovers secret

// Enables encryption-like abstraction without crypto
// Rights amplification pattern
```

## 9.1 OVERVIEW: WHY SESSION TYPES?

Session types provide **type-level protocols** for communication:

```

Ã¢â€â€š THE PROBLEM: Communication Safety                                               Ã¢â€â€š
Ã¢â€Å“Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€â‚¬Ã¢â€Â¤
Ã¢â€â€š                                                                                 Ã¢â€â€š
Ã¢â€â€š Traditional types ensure:                                                       Ã¢â€â€š
Ã¢â€â€š   Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Data has correct shape (int, string, struct)                               Ã¢â€â€š
```

**Connection to TERAS:**
- Network protocols in security systems need correctness guarantees
- eKYC (BENTENG) has multi-step verification protocols
- Digital signature workflows (SANDI) have complex state machines
- Threat sharing (SARAF mesh) requires protocol correctness

# PART X: PRE-PHASE MANDATES

## Decision Details by Domain

### Type Theory (D1-D4)

```
D1: Universe Structure
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Use predicative hierarchy: TypeÃ¢â€šâ‚¬ : TypeÃ¢â€šÂ : TypeÃ¢â€šâ€š : ...
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Prop universe for proof-irrelevant propositions
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Consider impredicativity for Prop only (like Coq)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Universe polymorphism for library code

D2: Dependent Types
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Full ÃŽÂ -types (dependent functions)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Full ÃŽÂ£-types (dependent pairs)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Identity types with J-eliminator
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Consider HoTT-style equality later

D3: Inductive Types
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Positive inductive types with eliminators
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Pattern matching as derived form
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Termination checking via structural recursion
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Guard condition similar to Coq

D4: Computation
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Strong normalization required
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ ÃŽÂ²-reduction as primary computation rule
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ ÃŽÂ·-expansion for functions and pairs
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Definitional vs propositional equality distinction
```

### Linear Types (D5-D9)

```
D5: Linear Type System
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Affine by default (use at most once)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Linear annotation for "must use exactly once"
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Unrestricted annotation for copyable types

D6: Ownership Model
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Single owner principle (like Rust)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Move semantics by default
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Borrowing for temporary access
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Mutable borrows exclusive

D7: Lifetime System
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Region-based lifetimes
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit when needed, elided when unambiguous
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ NLL-style flow-sensitive analysis

D8: Comptime Integration
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Compile-time function execution (like Zig)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Type-level computation
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Comptime parameters for generics

D9: Safety Guarantees
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Memory safety by default (no null, no dangling)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Bounds checking in debug mode
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Overflow checking configurable
```

### Refinement Types (D10-D14)

```
D10: Refinement Type Integration
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Refinement types as primary specification mechanism
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ { v : T | Ãâ€  } syntax for refined types
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Measures for inductively defined functions

D11: SMT Integration Strategy
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Multi-prover architecture (not single SMT dependency)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Primary: Z3, CVC5, Alt-Ergo
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Fallback: Coq for complex proofs
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Proof strategy system like Why3

D12: Decidability Boundary
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Liquid types subset for full inference
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ General refinements with manual proofs
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Clear annotation when leaving decidable fragment

D13: Ghost Code
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Ghost qualifier for specification-only code
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Erased at compile time
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Cannot affect runtime behavior

D14: Loop Invariants & Termination
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Explicit loop invariants required
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Termination metrics (variants)
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Default termination checking
```

### Memory & Verification (D15-D22)

```
D15-D18: Memory Model
Ã¢â‚¬Â¢ Separation logic as semantic foundation
```

## Track A: Memory Models & Effect Systems

### 0.5-A1: Memory Models Ã¢â‚¬â€ Foundations

**Objective:** Establish formal understanding of memory models for concurrent/distributed systems.

**Topics:**
- Sequential consistency model
- Release-acquire semantics
- C/C++ memory model
- Rust memory model (including atomics)
- Hardware memory models (x86-TSO, ARM, RISC-V)

**Output:** Memory Model Foundation Report (MMFR)

### 0.5-A2: Memory Models Ã¢â‚¬â€ Weak Models & Formalization

**Objective:** Deep dive into weak memory models and their formal treatment.

**Topics:**
- Relaxed memory ordering
- Memory barriers and fences
- Promising Semantics
- Operational vs axiomatic models
- Model checking for weak memory

**Output:** Weak Memory Formalization Report (WMFR)

### 0.5-A3: Memory Models Ã¢â‚¬â€ Verification Implications Ã¢â€ â€™ D39

**Objective:** Determine how memory model choice affects verification.

**Topics:**
- Program logic under weak memory
- Separation logic extensions
- Verification tool survey
- TERAS requirements alignment

**Output:** Memory Model Decision (D39)

### 0.5-A4: Effect Systems Ã¢â‚¬â€ Foundations

**Objective:** Survey effect system designs for TERAS integration.

**Topics:**
- Monadic effects (Haskell IO)
- Algebraic effects (Eff, Koka, OCaml 5)
- Effect polymorphism
- Row-polymorphic effects
- Effect handlers

**Output:** Effect Systems Survey Report (ESSR)

### 0.5-A5: Effect Systems Ã¢â‚¬â€ Advanced & Integration Ã¢â€ â€™ D40

**Objective:** Design effect system that integrates with TERAS type features.

**Topics:**
- Effect + linear type interaction
- Effect + refinement type interaction
- Effect + session type interaction
- Effect erasure and optimization

**Output:** Effect System Decision (D40)

## Track B: Product Requirements Analysis

### 0.5-P1 through 0.5-P5: Product-Specific Requirements

Each session extracts language requirements from one TERAS product:

| Session | Product | Output | Key Language Requirements |
|---------|---------|--------|---------------------------|
| 0.5-P1 | MENARA | MRD | KerisMesh types, mobile constraints, PINQ query types |
| 0.5-P2 | GAPURA | GRD | eBPF compilation, packet processing types, WAF rule DSL |
| 0.5-P3 | ZIRAH | ZRD | Behavioral monitoring types, rule engine DSL |
| 0.5-P4 | BENTENG | BRD | Biometric types, eKYC protocol types, liveness proofs |
| 0.5-P5 | SANDI | SRD | Signature types, algorithm agility, compliance proofs |

### 0.5-P5.5: BENTENG-SDK Requirements Analysis Ã¢â€ â€™ BSRD

**Objective:** Extract requirements for client-side SDK in hostile environment.

**Topics:**
1. Cross-platform compilation (iOS, Android, Web, Desktop)
2. Hostile environment defense (SDK in untrusted app)
3. Proof-carrying code requirements
4. FFI safety requirements
5. Size constraints (<5MB mobile, <1MB WASM)
6. API surface constraints
7. Performance in embedded context

**Output:** BENTENG-SDK Requirements Document (BSRD)

### 0.5-P6: TERAS Architecture Requirements Ã¢â€ â€™ ARD

**Objective:** Extract requirements from TERAS's revolutionary architecture.

**Topics:**
1. SARAF patterns (distributed command mesh)
2. NADI patterns (BFT pulse network)
3. JEJAK patterns (append-only audit)
4. Collective Immunity (BENTENG KEKEBALAN)
5. Algorithm agility requirements
6. Cross-product coordination

**Output:** Architecture Requirements Document (ARD)

### 0.5-P7: Cross-Product Integration Requirements Ã¢â€ â€™ CIRD

**Objective:** Analyze how TERAS products interact and share types.

**Topics:**
1. Product interaction map (MENARAÃ¢â€ â€BENTENG, GAPURAÃ¢â€ â€ZIRAH, etc.)
2. Shared type requirements (identity, threat, crypto types)
3. Protocol interoperability
4. Trust boundaries between products
5. Coordination patterns
6. Deployment topology impact

**Output:** Cross-Product Integration Requirements Document (CIRD)

## Track C: Threat Analysis

### 0.5-T1: Complete Threat Taxonomy Ã¢â€ â€™ TTD, D41

**Objective:** Create exhaustive taxonomy of security threats TERAS-LANG must address.

**Categories:**
- Memory safety threats (buffer overflow, use-after-free, etc.)
- Type confusion threats
- Cryptographic threats (side channels, weak RNG, etc.)
- Protocol threats (MITM, replay, etc.)
- Injection threats (SQL, command, etc.)
- Supply chain threats

**Output:** Threat Taxonomy Document (TTD), D41

### 0.5-T2: Threat-Feature Mapping Ã¢â€ â€™ TDM, D42

**Objective:** Map each threat to defending language feature.

**Matrix Structure:**
| Threat Class | Defense Feature | Defense Level |
|--------------|-----------------|---------------|
| Buffer overflow | Dependent types + bounds | Impossible |
| Use-after-free | Linear types | Impossible |
| Data race | Session types + linear | Impossible |
| Timing side channel | CT types | Compile-time |

**Output:** Threat-Defense Matrix (TDM), D42

### 0.5-T3: Future Threat Modeling Ã¢â€ â€™ FTDS, D43, D44

**Objective:** Anticipate threats TERAS-LANG must be prepared for.

**Topics:**
- Post-quantum cryptography transition
- AI-assisted attacks
- New side channel classes
- Emerging vulnerability patterns

**Output:** Future Threat Defense Strategy (FTDS), D43, D44

### 0.5-T4: Attack Surface Analysis Ã¢â€ â€™ ASB, D45

**Objective:** Analyze TERAS-LANG's own attack surface.

**Attack Vectors:**
- Compiler attacks
- Type system unsoundness
- SMT solver exploits
- Supply chain for language tooling
- IDE/tooling attacks

**Output:** Attack Surface Boundaries (ASB), D45

## Track D: Performance Foundations

### 0.5-PERF: Performance Requirements Synthesis Ã¢â€ â€™ UPR, D47

**Objective:** Synthesize performance requirements from all products.

**Topics:**
1. Per-product performance requirements
2. Unified Performance Requirements (UPR)
3. Benchmark suite design
4. Performance verification strategy

**Output:** Unified Performance Requirements (UPR), D47

# PART XIII: PHASE 1 ROADMAP

## Overview

**Phase 1: LANGUAGE DESIGN**
- Total Sessions: 30
- Decisions: D48-D100 (53 decisions)
- Purpose: Complete language specification

## Foundation Layer (Sessions 1-1 through 1-4)

### 1-1: Core Calculus Definition Ã¢â€ â€™ D48, D49, D50

**Decisions:**
- D46: Malay naming convention (pre-approved)
- D51: Layout rules (braces vs indentation)
- D52: Operator precedence

### 1-PROD-7: TERAS Architecture DSL Layer Ã¢â€ â€™ D97, D98, D99, D100

**Objective:** DSL for TERAS's revolutionary architecture patterns.

**Topics:**
1. SARAF Patterns (distributed command mesh)
   - Command distribution types
   - Consensus primitives
   - Mesh topology types

2. NADI Patterns (BFT pulse network)
   - Health check types
   - Byzantine fault tolerance
   - Quorum types

3. JEJAK Patterns (append-only audit)
   - Immutable log types
   - Tamper evidence
   - Audit query DSL

4. Algorithm Agility Patterns
   - Hot-swap crypto types
   - Migration protocols
   - Compatibility verification

**Decisions:**
- D97: SARAF pattern syntax
- D98: NADI pattern syntax
- D99: JEJAK pattern syntax
- D100: Algorithm agility syntax

## Threat Defense Layer (Sessions 1-DEF-1 through 1-DEF-3)

### 1-DEF-1: Defense-in-Depth Architecture

**Objective:** Implement D37 threat defense mandate in language design.

### 1-DEF-2: Constant-Time Enforcement

**Objective:** Extend D30 with comprehensive constant-time verification.

### 1-DEF-3: Attack Surface Minimization

**Objective:** Apply 0.5-T4 attack surface analysis to minimize language attack surface.

---


# PART XIV: DEPENDENCY GRAPH

# PART XVI: OPEN QUESTIONS

## Phase 0.5 Open Questions (to be resolved)

| ID | Question | Session | Impact |
|----|----------|---------|--------|
| OQ-01 | Exact memory model choice (SC-DRF vs relaxed) | 0.5-A3 | Core calculus |
| OQ-02 | Algebraic vs monadic effects | 0.5-A5 | Effect system |
| OQ-03 | ZK proving time feasibility for mobile | 0.5-P4 | BENTENG-SDK |
| OQ-04 | Post-quantum algorithm selection | 0.5-T3 | Crypto primitives |
| OQ-05 | Trust model for collective immunity | 0.5-P6 | Architecture |

## Phase 1 Open Questions (anticipated)

| ID | Question | Session | Impact |
|----|----------|---------|--------|
| OQ-06 | Dependent type inference boundary | 1-3 | Usability |
| OQ-07 | Effect handler performance | 1-7 | Performance |
| OQ-08 | Can PCC proofs be generated automatically? | 1-PROD-4.5 | BENTENG-SDK |
| OQ-09 | FFI safety check overhead | 1-14 | Performance |
| OQ-10 | SDK async API design | 1-PROD-4.5 | API surface |
| OQ-11 | Cross-product protocol static verification | 1-PROD-7 | Verification |
| OQ-12 | Trust model between products | 0.5-P7 | Security |
| OQ-13 | Product version skew handling | 0.5-P7 | Compatibility |

## Design Questions (Future Phases)

1. **Syntax Design**: What should TERAS-LANG look like?
2. **Error Messages**: How to make dependent type errors understandable?
3. **IDE Integration**: How to provide good tooling from start?
4. **Incremental Compilation**: How to handle dependent types incrementally?
5. **FFI Design**: How to interface with C/Rust safely?

# PART XVII: BIBLIOGRAPHY & SOURCES

## Type Theory

- Martin-LÃƒÂ¶f, P. (1984). Intuitionistic Type Theory
- Coquand, T. & Huet, G. (1988). The Calculus of Constructions
- Paulin-Mohring, C. (1989). Extracting Programs from Proofs
- The Univalent Foundations Program (2013). Homotopy Type Theory

## Linear Types

- Girard, J-Y. (1987). Linear Logic
- Wadler, P. (1990). Linear Types Can Change the World
- Walker, D. (2005). Substructural Type Systems
- Bernardy, J-P. et al. (2018). Linear Haskell: Practical Linearity in a Higher-order Polymorphic Language

## Refinement Types

- Vazou, N. et al. (2014). Refinement Types for Haskell
- Swamy, N. et al. (2016). Dependent Types and Multi-Monadic Effects in F*
- Lehmann, N. et al. (2023). Flux: Liquid Types for Rust
- Jhala, R. & Vazou, N. (2021). Refinement Types: A Tutorial

## Separation Logic

- Reynolds, J. (2002). Separation Logic: A Logic for Shared Mutable Data Structures
- O'Hearn, P. (2004). Resources, Concurrency, and Local Reasoning
- Jung, R. et al. (2018). Iris from the Ground Up
- Jung, R. et al. (2017). RustBelt: Securing the Foundations of the Rust Programming Language

## Verified Compilers

- Leroy, X. (2009). Formal Verification of a Realistic Compiler
- Kumar, R. et al. (2014). CakeML: A Verified Implementation of ML
- Stewart, G. et al. (2015). Compositional CompCert

## Zero-Knowledge

- Groth, J. (2016). On the Size of Pairing-based Non-interactive Arguments
- Gabizon, A. et al. (2019). PLONK: Permutations over Lagrange-bases for Oecumenical Noninteractive arguments of Knowledge
- Ben-Sasson, E. et al. (2018). Scalable, Transparent, and Post-quantum Secure Computational Integrity
- Circom, Noir, Leo, Cairo language documentation

## Security

- Denning, D. & Denning, P. (1977). Certification of Programs for Secure Information Flow
- Miller, M. (2006). Robust Composition: Towards a Unified Approach to Access Control and Concurrency Control
- Myers, A. & Liskov, B. (1997). A Decentralized Model for Information Flow Control
- Sabelfeld, A. & Myers, A. (2003). Language-based Information-flow Security

## Session Types

- Honda, K. (1993). Types for Dyadic Interaction
- Honda, K., Yoshida, N. & Carbone, M. (2008). Multiparty Asynchronous Session Types
- Caires, L. & Pfenning, F. (2010). Session Types as Intuitionistic Linear Propositions
- Toninho, B. et al. (2011). Dependent Session Types via Intuitionistic Linear Logic
- Yoshida, N. & Vasconcelos, V. (2007). Language Primitives and Type Discipline for Structured Communication
- Scalas, A. & Yoshida, N. (2019). Less is More: Multiparty Session Types Revisited

## Effect Systems

- Lucassen, J. & Gifford, D. (1988). Polymorphic Effect Systems
- Plotkin, G. & Power, J. (2003). Algebraic Operations and Generic Effects
- Bauer, A. & Pretnar, M. (2015). Programming with Algebraic Effects and Handlers
- Leijen, D. (2017). Type Directed Compilation of Row-typed Algebraic Effects

## Memory Models

- Sewell, P. et al. (2010). x86-TSO: A Rigorous and Usable Programmer's Model for x86 Multiprocessors
- Batty, M. et al. (2011). Mathematizing C++ Concurrency
- Kang, J. et al. (2017). A Promising Semantics for Relaxed-Memory Concurrency
